commit 57c2cef61cecde2a7ee2a2454f55bcdce709a9d6
Author: idimopoulos <idimopoulos@hotmail.com>
Date:   Tue Oct 4 22:14:15 2016 +0200

    ISAICP-2603: Adding to the last large commit.
    When you change the idea of a functionality, make sure the pattern applies to the whole code.
    I changed the order of the foreach loops.
    
    Before, we were looping first through the graphs and then through the entities.
    Now we are looping first through the entities and then through the graphs.
    
    Before we were returning in case a graph was valid within the first loop because we were satisfied by the results of one graph.
    Now we should not return because otherwise we skip entities, NOT graphs. Add an if clause to continue instead.
    
    I am never surpised my my ability to build patterns and my stupidity that leaves blank spots behind...

commit 4304ff013f1c3aae85f5146d64b5373486dfd933
Author: idimopoulos <idimopoulos@hotmail.com>
Date:   Tue Oct 4 19:39:40 2016 +0200

    ISAICP-2603: :(.. Rewrite process results.
    The idea here is that there was a bug with the request graphs. The priority of the request graphs was not respected.
    What changed is that the entity graphs are loaded for the entity type and then are filtered for each priority graph.
    The issue is that we have the request graph ids but we get the results indexed by graph uris.
    To fill the gap, we are loading the full list of the graphs.
    
    WARNING: This might cause issues if multiple graphs for multiple bundles are defining the same uri.
    E.g. If a bundle 1 has a default graph http://uri1 and a draft graph http://uri2
    and a bundle 2 has a default graph http://uri2 and a draft graph http://uri3
    and the graph draft is requested for an entity, if it is of a type bundle 1 then the wrong graph will
    be loaded.
    This is caused because the query must be bundle agnostic for the cases that a bundle is not provided
    so all bundles are taken into account.
